Tao Baichuan Reports on His Inspection of Various European and American Countries at the Expanded Memorial Week at the City Government Yesterday

Tao Baichuan, a standing committee member of the City Party Headquarters, went to the United States to study last year and visited various European and American countries. He returned to Shanghai last month. Mayor Wu specially convened officials from various bureaus at the City Government Auditorium yesterday to hold an expanded memorial week and invited Tao to report on his inspection. His report is recorded as follows:

United States: Chairman, comrades, I went to the United States last year to study and achieved my lifelong wish. I also took the opportunity to travel to various European countries. I will report what I saw to you. I spent a longer time in the United States. As you know, the United States is the land of gold, but what I saw in the United States is completely different from the ideal land of gold. Everywhere in the United States, you can see idlers. Even in New York, there are beggars. This is indeed affected by the global economic recession. Among the 120 million people in the United States, there are 12 million unemployed, accounting for one-tenth, which is a serious situation. The government's method of helping the unemployed is either giving money or giving work. Therefore, the government's expenditure is very large. Last year, the federal government's budget was 4 billion US dollars, the state governments' budget was 2 billion US dollars, and the county and village governments' budget was 6 billion US dollars, totaling 12 billion US dollars in government expenses per year. China only has 900 million yuan per year. The source of government expenses, of course, comes from the people. Therefore, the average American bears 100 US dollars in government expenses per year. The land of gold has also begun to show signs of poverty. Moreover, because the US government helps the unemployed, it cannot assign people according to their abilities, so the political efficiency is very low. However, the efficiency of private enterprises such as factories and shops is very high.

England: After living in the United States for more than a year, I went to England. I felt that the political efficiency in England was higher than that in the United States, but the standard of living and the material enjoyment of the people were lower than in the United States. The British are quite able to do things step by step and seek truth from facts, unlike the Americans who like to reach for the sky and be startled by the distance. In the schools in the United States, sometimes very good school buildings or gardens are demolished and rebuilt. The reason for this is said to be that frequent demolition and construction can circulate wealth, so that architects, engineers, workers, and lumber mills and other factories have business to do. The United States does indeed burn or sink wheat into the sea in order to balance prices. England is quite able to save.

Denmark: From England to Denmark, Denmark gave me a deep impression. The Danish people are very happy and there are no thieves. Denmark has over 800,000 people, and there are only 900 policemen in the whole country, accounting for one in a thousand. Therefore, you cannot see policemen on the road. The reason for this is that the people live and work in peace and have no need for policemen. Shanghai's policemen account for 2%, and other countries also have at least 2%. The reason why Denmark has achieved this is due to the development of the cooperative system. There are no extremely rich or extremely poor classes. The people's lives are all above the level.

Sweden: The buildings of the Swedish city government are often magnificent and rare. Their cost is equivalent to 35 million Chinese currency. Construction took 12 years to complete and is the first in the world. However, the Swedish royal palace is not so magnificent. It is said that the city government's building is so great because it is a way to absorb the economy. Because it is the world's first, many tourists come to Sweden to visit the city government, so that the commercial center can be developed. Therefore, the merchants invested the most in the construction of the city government, which can attract tourists and attract business. It can be seen that the source of wealth is not necessarily the mining industry, the scenery is also one of the sources of wealth.

Finland: In Finland, it is rare to see asphalt roads and cement roads. Most of them are stone roads, because the country is very poor. However, among the European countries, only Greece and Finland, these two small countries, can repay the war debts to the United States every year. Therefore, they have a high position in the international community. In this world conference, when discussing the location for the next meeting, Finland also participated in the struggle. This is rare among the emerging countries in Europe.

Soviet Russia: In Leningrad, the Soviet customs inspection is very strict. You cannot bring books, and the money you carry with you must also be reported. The people's lives are very difficult, but they are very content. The Soviet workers' monthly income is only 140 rubles, which is not enough to buy a pair of leather shoes, but the workers say that they have social wages, such as schools, libraries, sports fields, etc. Especially the Red Army, supporting the Red Army is their biggest job. The power of propaganda is really great. I think the maintenance of a dictatorship requires at least four conditions: (1) military force, (2) a private party, (3) official propaganda, and (4) bestowing favors on people. The situation in Soviet Russia is also like this. Now, analyzing the people's lives in the world, there are four lines: (1) starvation line, (2) subsistence line, (3) savings line, (4) extravagance line. Some countries have the extravagance line and also the starvation line. Soviet Russia has nothing on the extravagance line and nothing on the starvation line. The people all have food to eat, because Soviet Russia's production is aimed at feeding the people.

Germany: From Poland to Germany, Germany is a country of air force nationalism, which is completely different from the United States. After Hitler came to power, he added a new association that "young people can resolve disputes through duels." Therefore, whoever has scars on their body is a hero. Girls mostly worship heroes. Elementary school students carry knives and swords, unlike the United States, where recruiting soldiers requires a large movement, making slides and projecting them to promote how pleasant life is as a soldier, but very few are willing to be soldiers.

France: The situation in France is different from the others. The society is full of luxurious phenomena. France's annual consumption of champagne reaches 50 million yuan, not including wine. Prostitutes, both private and public, are everywhere. Therefore, some people use two "W"s to describe France: Wine and Woman. Its licentiousness and enjoyment are rarely seen in other countries.

Italy: Italy is a country that is quite energetic and spirited. It is indeed a revitalizing country. Mussolini himself has no drawers on his desk, so as not to delay official business. Moreover, he collects the important official business every day and brings back the unfinished business the next day to warn the person in charge not to imprison official business. This can be seen from this. The people's patriotism is quite tense.

Conclusion: China's national revival can use two slogans: (1) Save it from the root, (2) Catch up from the front. Saving it from the root must start from people's training, economic development must start from the basics, and if we can catch up from the front, we will not be left behind. Therefore, the New Life Movement promoted by Chairman Chiang, as well as the National Economic Construction Movement, and quick action, practical work, and hard work are the ways to save the country. The New Life Movement is people's training, and the National Economic Construction Movement is seeking economic development, which is the way to save from the root. Quick action, practical work, and hard work are the methods to catch up from the front.

Industrial and Commercial Loan Committee to End in Autumn Next Year, Over 700,000 Yuan in Uncollected Funds, Last Batch Due in September Next Year

The Municipal Industrial and Commercial Loan Review Committee was established last year at the request of the industrial and commercial circles and was jointly established by the Bank of China, the Bank of Communications, and the China National Products Bank, with a total capital of 5 million yuan. The Ministry of Finance appointed Cai Zengji and others as members to oversee the loan affairs. It has been over a year and four months since then. After passing the last batch of loans on the 3rd of last month, it was ordered by the ministry to stop handling them. Since the Ministry of Finance implemented the new currency system policy, and with the solid efforts of the banking industry, finance has been stabilized, and the monetary policy has gradually loosened. Banks and money shops have large sums of money to lend, so the committee is no longer necessary. According to a reporter, after the committee was established, it held monthly meetings to review and handle loan applications. The most applications were from textile factories. Others, such as those running small factories and shops, were more scattered. The committee stipulated very strict conditions, and the total amount of loans per household was also limited to 5,000 yuan. Therefore, the total amount of loans issued has only reached over 900,000 yuan. Apart from the 100,000 yuan that has been collected, the amount of loans currently issued is about 700,000 yuan. They will be collected on a monthly basis when they are due. When the last batch is due for collection in September next year, the committee will be dissolved.

Shanghai Silk Factories Run Out of Raw Materials, Shaoxing Silk Factory Stops Production, Zhejiang Unified Control Association's Spring Cocoons Difficult to Sell, Chinese Silk Prices Soar, Sales Turn Smooth

Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces suffer from poor autumn cocoon harvests. Shanghai silk factories are running out of raw materials and have stopped production one after another. They are hoping that the Zhejiang Sericulture Unified Control Association will sell the spring cocoons in stock at a fair price. Exports of Chinese silk have turned smooth, and prices have soared. The details are as follows:

Raw Materials Are Exhausted

There are a total of 48 silk factories in the Zhabei, Nanshi, and concession areas of Shanghai, including Ewo, Jiyu, Hengcang, etc., with a total of 11,000 machines. Since the autumn cocoons in Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces were poor, the Wuxi Yongtai Silk Factory bought a large amount of leftover cocoons, resulting in a shortage of leftover cocoons on the market. The silk factories are all feeling panicked due to the lack of raw materials. The Shaoxing Silk Factory in Zhabei stopped production the day before yesterday due to the exhaustion of raw materials. As for the factories that are still operating, the maximum amount of raw materials is only enough for two months.

Zhejiang Cocoons Difficult to Sell

The silk factories are aware that stopping production due to the lack of raw materials affects the livelihoods of tens of thousands of workers. They all hope that the Zhejiang Sericulture Unified Control Association will sell the spring cocoons it has collected to the Shanghai silk factories at a fair price, so that they can continue to operate and produce silk. However, the spring cocoons collected by the Zhejiang Sericulture Unified Control Association have already been managed by the silk reeling committee, which entrusted the Hangzhou Silk Factory and others to reel the silk, and the sales committee sold it overseas. Now it has been dumped in advance, so a fair price sale is unlikely to be achieved.

Silk Sales Turn Smooth

Chinese silk in the European and American markets had previously plummeted in price and sales were almost cut off due to the dumping of Japanese silk. Domestic silk factories' users have sharply reduced transactions due to the tense situation. Since last week, the prices of Chinese silk have soared abroad and now it is up to 1.73 US dollars, equivalent to about 690 yuan in national currency, and sales have turned smooth. Domestic silk factory users have increased sales compared to before because the rumors have subsided. As for the silk merchants in Shanghai, they do not dare to sell futures due to the lack of raw materials, fearing that they will not be able to deliver the goods at that time.

Ma Yinchu Discusses Improving the Bank Guarantee System

According to the New Voice News Agency, cases of embezzlement and fraud are very numerous in society nowadays. As reported recently, there are pursuit cases of embezzlement, fraud, and cheating at the American-China Bank, the Trust and Easy Trust Company, and the China Industrial Bank. This trend is growing daily. According to a certain statistician, there were 43 cases of fraud in the financial sector last year, amounting to more than 1.68 million yuan, which can be regarded as a serious social problem. When the famous economist Dr. Ma Yinchu met with a reporter, he expressed his feelings as follows: "The current guarantee system in China's professional circles has always used individual and shop guarantees. This type of system is not practical in many ways under the current complex social economy and has many drawbacks. After embezzlement cases occur, guarantors can rarely fulfill the original purpose of the guarantee compensation. To guarantee for others requires unlimited liability, and people are afraid to try, wanting to help but being burdened instead. Therefore, employees feel it is extremely difficult to find a guarantor. This is especially true in the banking sector. We have seen repeated cases of embezzlement and fraud being prosecuted over the years, and there is no way to curb them. Therefore, improving the guarantee system is the unanimous expectation of all sectors of society. However, how to improve it is a matter that requires much research. According to people in the financial sector, a certain bank has a proposal to abolish the current guarantee system and suggest a 'Special Cash Guarantee Method.' I recently saw the regulations, which use a considerable amount of cash as a guarantee and adopt the spirit of insurance, while also embodying the beauty of savings, consisting of three types of guarantee deposits (A, B, and C) and five principles: joint and several punishment, reward for reporting, and so on. This deposit contains the nature of a guarantee. If there is no embezzlement, it can still be returned. Its role is that all employees have a personal stake in it, which can encourage each other and eliminate the occurrence of bad events. This method embodies the spirit of group mutual assistance and cooperation, is more practical and reasonable than the simple guarantor system, and its meaning is worlds apart. It also complies with the scientific management of personnel. In modern times, all countries strive to improve the credit guarantee business and implement it practically. However, although the premiums paid by various institutions to domestic and foreign insurance companies for credit insurance are huge, they do not have a positive effect. I have observed that the 'Special Cash Guarantee Method' suggested by a certain bank, the Type A guarantee deposit is based on the British model, the Type B guarantee deposit is based on the American model, and the Type C guarantee deposit is based on China's situation. The entire method is roughly similar to the current guarantee system of the (National Provincial Bank Ltd, London) bank in England. The abolition of China's current bank guarantor system is undoubtedly necessary. However, reforming a certain system requires thorough research and then implementing it with a firm spirit, such as the government's abolition of taels and change of currency system, which are precedents. I sincerely hope that people in China's financial circles will pay attention to this issue and seek the best possible solution, implement it practically, or have one bank promote it alone, or several banks jointly handle it. Isn't it fortunate for both employees and guarantors?"

Shen Yiqian's Wife Died After Childbirth, Accuses Midwife of Negligence, Midwife States What Happened, The Case Has Been Tried and the Verdict Will be Announced on the 29th

Shen Yiqian, a native of Wujiang who lives at 11, Lane 182, Tongfu Road, Public Concession, is 38 years old. His wife, Shen Zhuxiuzhen, gave birth to a girl on the 29th of last month. Xu Xiuying (36 years old), a female obstetrician from Changshu at 17, Dongchunhua Lane 59, Juberlais Road, French Concession, was hired to deliver the baby. On the fourth day after delivery, she suddenly developed a fever and chills and sought medical treatment. It was believed that Xu did not disinfect properly during delivery, causing bacteria to infect the uterus, turning into endometritis and peritonitis. She was sent to Tongde Hospital for treatment but was ineffective and died on the night of Double Ten Festival. Later, Shen Yiqian discovered that Xu Xiuying was a midwife who impersonated an obstetrician, published diagnostic examples, and also engaged in gynecology and smoking cessation. She was suspected of forging documents, fraudulently obtaining property, and not disinfecting the delivery surgery properly, causing the pregnant woman to become ill and die. He filed a complaint with the Criminal Court of the Special Second Court against Xu Xiuying for forgery, fraud, and professional negligence resulting in death, requesting investigation. According to the complaint, the court yesterday summoned him to the Second Criminal Court by Judge Chen Shuoying. First, the plaintiff Shen Yiqian stated the intent of his complaint and presented a paper diagnostic example of the defendant printed in red paper impersonating a physician, requesting interrogation based on Article 215, Article 276, Paragraph 2, and Article 340 of the Criminal Law. The defendant Xu Xiuying arrived in court with her defense lawyer. She stated that the plaintiff's wife's delivery was introduced by the neighbor Shen Shuai's mother. She first registered on September 17 and paid 2 yuan. On the morning of the 28th, I went to deliver the baby and charged a total of 16 yuan for delivery and medicine. The mother and daughter were safe after delivery. I went to see her early every day, and there was nothing unusual. When I went to see her on the fourth morning, the pregnant woman said she had a fever and chills. I immediately said that I was a midwife, not a doctor, and that she should seek medical treatment from another doctor. The plaintiff did not listen and gave herself injections and enemas. Later, I introduced Dr. Wang Shuzhen to see her and told them to send her to the hospital quickly. I disinfected completely during delivery and was not negligent. As for the physician printed on the diagnostic examples, it was because there was a specialized physician at home to treat the illness. I am a midwife and did not impersonate a physician. She also presented a registration certificate from the Health Bureau and filed a counter-lawsuit accusing the plaintiff of slander. The court believed that the facts were clear, ordered the debate to be opened, and then announced the end, scheduling the verdict to be announced on the 29th.

Pudong Water Plant Will Supply Water by the End of the Year

Water Pipeline Project Will Be Completed

In order to prosper the Pudong market and make it convenient for citizens to use water, the Municipal Industrial Trust Society has allocated funds to operate the Pudong Water Plant. Since the site near Youlong Wharf in Pudong was surveyed and the construction of the plant buildings was tendered last autumn, all the buildings of the new plant have been completed in the spring, and all internal machinery, water tanks, and other projects have also been arranged and completed. According to the original plan, water was originally planned to be opened for supply in September this year. However, because the streets of Pudong are curved and not straight, the underground water pipeline project was quite tortuous. Even many places had pipelines running into the households or the stratum of the warehouses. The trouble of the project was unparalleled. The society has invested heavily in the Pudong Water Plant, but as a municipal agency, the purpose is to facilitate the citizens. The unexpected losses will not be counted. Now the final project of burying the water pipes of the plant is about to be completed. The main and branch water pipes of each road will be connected to the main pipe of the water tank in the plant next month. Water supply will be opened no later than this year.

Suspended Chinese Constable Yan Xingpei Suspected of Fraud and Obtaining Money, Arrested and Detained by Gordon Road Police Station, Yan Scammed in the Name of Seeking Opportunities for Others

The General Inspectorate had suspended Chinese Constable No. 1966, Yan Xingpei (also known as Yan Xiangchen) from Anhui. He was arrested and detained by the Gordon Road Police Station a few days ago on suspicion of fraud and obtaining money. Yesterday morning, he was sent to the Second Criminal Division of the First Special Court. Police lawyer Qian Xunjiu filed a public prosecution according to Article 339 of the Criminal Law for the crime of fraud and obtaining money. Lawyer Qian also described the situation: The defendant Yan Xingpei used to be a Chinese constable and lived on the second floor of No. 875 Loulang Road in West Shanghai. His second landlord, Wang Liansheng, had a son named Shi Fa who was unemployed at home, so he asked the defendant to find him a job. The defendant took the opportunity to say that the Shanghai Brewery Company was currently in need of people and that he could recommend him, but that a "lobbying fee" of 20 yuan was required. Wang Liansheng, eager to find a job, paid the amount in full. Unexpectedly, after many days, there was no news. When Wang contacted Yan, Yan immediately returned the 30 yuan he had received in full. A few days later, the defendant suddenly claimed that he was now a translator in the Police Affairs Department of the General Inspectorate and that the Municipal Council was recruiting probationary constables and he could intercede on his behalf, but demanded a "lobbying fee" of 150 yuan. Wang agreed and said that it would be paid in three installments. Wang was short of money, so he borrowed 70 yuan from his friend Liu Caigui, and together with the previous 20 yuan for the brewery company, he made up 100 yuan. On March 13th and 16th of this year, he paid 50 yuan each time. The remaining 50 yuan would be paid after the matter was settled. On March 18th, the defendant suddenly moved elsewhere on some pretext. Although Wang repeatedly urged the defendant, he always avoided him. In May, Wang suddenly received a notice from the Municipal Council ordering him to go to the General Inspectorate writing room for an exam. The notice was stamped with the Municipal Council's seal. Wang was overjoyed, thinking that the job was done, and hurriedly asked the defendant. Unexpectedly, the defendant suddenly said that the letter was probably not genuine and suggested looking for another job. He said that he was familiar with a Westerner named Yin Sigui at the Shanghai Electric Army Company and could introduce him to a permanent position, but the result was another pie in the sky. At this point, Wang realized that the defendant was a con artist. It was not until yesterday that he caught him on the road and sent him to the police station. However, the defendant denied receiving 100 yuan at the police station, saying that he was being framed by Wang out of spite because Wang's mother had a relationship with a mutual friend. He requested a lawyer to come to court and request bail. Judge Pan Zhenyang ordered the defendant to be detained and the hearing rescheduled for this Friday.

Western Paint Industry Lawsuit, Witnesses Interrogated Yesterday, Landlord and Tenant Both Appeared in Court, Court Inquires About Purchase Books from Ten Years Ago

Ma Shangjie, representative of the Shanghai Western Paint Industry Association, hired a lawyer to file a lawsuit in the Second Criminal Court against Le Zhenbao, Bei Runsheng, Zhang Lanping, Le Gengrong, and others for managing the property of the Yanghuo Commercial Association of Xinqiao Street. The details have been reported in previous newspapers. Yesterday was the date for the continued hearing. Both parties were accompanied by lawyers Chao Kun, Gao Danhua, Yan Yinwu, Li Zuyu, Lin Yingqing, Zai Manyun, and Yuan Hanyun to the court. At 2:30 PM, Judge Chen Shuoying and clerk Wang Baoxun arrived at the Second Criminal Court for the trial. The plaintiff's side presented evidence regarding the Yanghuo Commercial Association's collection of rent and the shortage of rent recorded for the tenant, Xin Kang Coal Store. Witnesses were summoned. First, Han Zikang, the owner of the Xin Kang Coal Store from Shaoxing, was questioned and ordered to provide a witness bond. According to Han's testimony, he had no relationship with the four defendants, but only rented their houses. He took over the store at 94-96 Xinqiao Street twenty years ago, which was two rooms, and rented them directly from the Yanghuo Association. The rent was 38 yuan per room per month, totaling 76 yuan. He paid the rent monthly with a rent book. Previously, the rent was collected by Pan Baolin, the accountant of the association, and now it is collected by Feng Minzeng. The rent for September was paid with a check for 76 yuan from Defeng Paint Store. The official asked Han about the note added to the evidence presented by the plaintiff Ma Shangjie, which said, "This check was borrowed from Defeng." You said today that you received goods from the exchange, which is obviously incorrect. What kind of check did you receive, a payment for goods or a borrowed check? Han replied that he had dealings with Defeng, only ten or so yuan per month, and the rest was borrowed from Defeng. He rented the house directly, not indirectly, and so on. Then, Feng Minzeng, the rent collector of the Yanghuo Association, testified that he was in charge of collecting rent at the Renyi Shan Association. He took over in the 22nd year of the Republic of China. The rent for Han Zikang's Xin Kang Coal Store was not collected by him. The house was rented to Zhu Zemin. He did not know when Zhu sublet it to Han. The rent was 56 yuan per month, sent by Zhang Shutang, with a rent ticket as proof. He presented a book of rent ticket stubs from January to September of this year for inspection. Zhang Shutang was also present in court today and could be summoned for questioning. The court immediately summoned Zhang Shutang, who testified that the houses at 94-96 Xinqiao Street were previously rented by his uncle Zhu Zemin. Zhu used to run a store himself, but due to the poor market and illness, he sublet the house to Han. There was a rent book. He was entrusted to collect the rent, 76 yuan per month. He paid 56 yuan to the landlord and held a rent ticket. At this point, he presented the rent book and rent ticket. He also said that he received a check for the rent in September and added more than 20 yuan to pay the landlord two months' rent. After examining the rent book, the court showed it to Han Zikang and asked if he paid the rent based on this book. After Han read it, he replied, "Yes." The official then asked, "The defendants ordered you to hand over the accounts, but you only submitted the account books for ten years starting from the fourteenth year. Where are the previous accounts?" Le Zhenbao replied that merchants, after receiving instructions, preserved account books for five years according to commercial practice. Now they have presented ten years. As for the previous accounts, they have to be checked. He couldn't say for sure if they were complete. At this point, the official ordered that Zhu Zemin, a witness, still needed to be summoned. The hearing was rescheduled for 3 PM on November 11th.

Fire at Qianye Primary School, Damage in Half an Hour is Not Small, No Accidents as Students Had Not Arrived

At about 8 AM yesterday morning, a fire suddenly broke out in the Qianye Primary School at the intersection of Wenjian Shi Road North and Henan Road. By the time it was discovered, it was beyond salvage. The Hongkou Fire Brigade received the news and immediately dispatched all firefighters and vehicles to put out the fire. Because the fire was raging, it was difficult to achieve results even after pouring water. Nearby residents were also greatly panicked, the noise was deafening, and the order was in chaos. After half an hour, the fire gradually subsided. As a result, all the school rooms were burned down, and the property was also lost a lot. Fortunately, no students had arrived at the school at the time, so there were no accidents. He was immediately sent to the hospital for treatment by car. The cause of the fire is currently being investigated by the police.

Crackdown on Extra Tips, This City Temporarily Suspended, Because the Market is Declining and the Situation is Special, It is Hoped That Labor and Management Will Automatically Rectify

Dagong News reported that the Shanghai New Life Movement Promotion Association had previously received an order from the General Association that taking extra tips in hotels, bathhouses, barbershops, restaurants, etc., was a bad habit and should be eliminated by formulating and implementing measures to ban extra tips. After receiving the order, the association believed that the situation in Shanghai was special and took a cautious approach. Considering the treatment of workers, it convened relevant parties several times for discussion, but there were no concrete results. The Shanghai Hotel Industry Association and others sent telegrams requesting a temporary suspension. The Dagong News reporter interviewed Jiang Hao, the secretary of the New Movement Association, yesterday. According to him, the crackdown on extra tips was originally intended to eliminate bad social habits and improve the personality of workers. However, the environment in this city is special. After repeated calls to representatives of labor and management from various agencies and industries, a careful implementation plan was developed. Now, the association believes that the market is declining and it is difficult for various industries to operate. If there is no appropriate protection for labor after the implementation of the ban, their livelihoods will be greatly affected. Therefore, it intends to submit a request to the General Association to temporarily not implement it in this city, or to allow labor and management in various industries to reform themselves. It is hoped that the capital side will adhere to the principle of small profits and quick turnover to effectively ban the extortion of tips, reduce the burden on customers, and emphasize social etiquette. It is also hoped that workers will respect their personality and no longer arbitrarily demand extra tips from customers. They must win the sympathy of customers with a respectful service spirit. The association will call relevant labor and management parties from various industries again in the coming days to earnestly persuade and faithfully implement this intention.

Paying for Soda with a Bad Check, Valued at Over 10,000 Yuan and Uncollectible When Due, Sun Renjie Arrested by Miao Yide and Taken to the Police Station

Sun Renjie, a man from Pudong, 40 years old, contacted Miao Yide, the accountant of the Tonghe Soda Company, the general distributor of Zheng Guanghe Soda Factory on Ningbo Road, in July of this year, and signed a contract to sell soda. He also established Datong Soda Company at No. 82 Guling Road. Up to September 5, he took away a total of 10,450 dozen sodas, valued at 11,551 yuan. Sun paid with seven checks from Pudong and Kenye Banks. When the checks were due, Miao could not collect the money, so he reported it to the Laozao Police Station. Detective Pang Ruiqing found that Sun had only deposited one or two hundred yuan in Pudong and Kenye Banks. He used the checks and then withdrew the remaining one or twenty yuan from the bank the next day. Therefore, the checks he paid to Miao were returned due to insufficient funds. The day before yesterday, Miao met Sun at the intersection of Chuqiao Road and Nanjing Road and took him to the police station. Yesterday morning, he was sent to the Second Court of the First Special Court. Police lawyer Qian Xunjiu filed a lawsuit in accordance with Article 339 of the Criminal Law, stating that the defendant confessed at the police station that he had sold some of the empty bottles to a man named Xu Naiwen, but there were still empty bottles worth more than 10,000 yuan that were unaccounted for. Therefore, he requested a postponement for investigation. When questioned, Sun Renjie confessed that he was the manager of Datong, contracted to sell soda with the plaintiff, and had a deed of 12,000 yuan and a business license as collateral. At that time, it was stipulated that each dozen would be 9 jiao, but the account was opened at 1 yuan per dozen. He had paid the plaintiff 1,000 yuan. Now, the market is bad, and it is difficult to collect accounts. It is even more difficult to collect all the empty bottles. He also hired lawyer Fan Gang to defend him. Judge Pan Zhenyang reviewed the confession and ordered a postponement for another hearing.

Liquidation of Cathay Bank Completed, Principal and Interest of 8 Million Yuan Paid, There Are Still Two Thousand Public Notices Urging Collection

After the temporary shareholders' meeting decided to liquidate the Cathay Bank in this city, the bank began to handle the liquidation procedures and has now come to an end. The details are as follows:

Organizational Content

Cathay Bank was established in August of the twelfth year, with a capital of 1 million yuan, fully paid at once. The location was No. 224 Tianjin Road. The chairman was Wang Boyuan, the managing directors were Zheng Bingquan and Xu Kecheng, the directors were Yu Zuoting, Xue Chunsheng, Sun Jieqing, Zhang Langqi, Xu Boxiong, Chen Shengwu, Liu Pinshan, and Lin Pingfu, and the supervisors were Wang Zhongyun, Feng Sicang, and Zhou Yongsheng. The general manager was Zheng Bingquan, the manager was Lin Pingfu, the deputy managers were Lou Gengru and Feng Qijun, and the assistant managers were Zheng Shufan and Zhang Gengsheng.

Liquidation Situation

All types of deposits in the bank, including various savings deposits, whether they were due or not, were refunded in full. The interest was calculated up to the day before the withdrawal. The principal and interest were all paid off. Currently, there are still some account holders who have not collected their money, totaling less than 2,000 yuan. Although it has been continuously advertised in newspapers for many days to urge collection, a liquidation office is still set up at No. 255 Beijing Road Yeda Building to wait for sporadic account holders to withdraw this thousand yuan of principal and interest in order to end the matter. During the bank's prosperous period, when there was a financial panic in Shanghai, the total amount of deposits was about 8 million yuan. Over the past year or so, the loans have been gradually collected and used to repay the deposits. Currently, there are still about 600,000 to 700,000 yuan of real estate and secure assets that have not yet expired, which will be gradually returned to shareholders' capital.

Notice to Collect

Respectfully, this bank passed a resolution at the second temporary shareholders' meeting on August 30th of this year to liquidate and entrust all directors of the board of directors as liquidators in each case. All fixed and current deposits in the Commercial Department and Savings Department, whether they are due or not, are requested to come to the bank immediately and calculate the principal and interest up to the day before the withdrawal. This notice is hereby advertised. We respectfully hope that all account holders will bring their deposit slips and follow the usual withdrawal procedures to withdraw their money.

The Hydrographic Office of this city stated that during the current low water period of the Yangtze River, the Zhenjiang-Nanjing section and the Wuhu-Anqing buoys have temporarily stopped illuminating. The announcements are listed below:

Announcement 1

Announcement No. 35, the "Liandong" buoy in the Zhenjiang-Nanjing section of the Yangtze River has temporarily stopped illuminating. Navigation Announcement No. 98 of this year should be repealed immediately. And, the azimuth of No. 76 is 8 degrees from Wulong Temple, a distance of 1.52 nautical miles, that is, approximately 118 degrees 52 minutes east longitude and 22 degrees 11 minutes north latitude. Description: During the low water period, the above-mentioned buoy will stop illuminating from the above-mentioned date. Original reporting agency: Jianghan Customs River Patrol Office.

Announcement 2

Arson Planned in Warehouse: Seven Russians Arrested; Large Fox Fur Valued at Over 400 Gold Coins Insured for a Huge Sum of 6,000 Yuan

In recent years, fires have occurred repeatedly in foreign warehouses storing goods in this city. The true cause of the fires has remained unknown. Although investigations were conducted, the results suggested arson, but no arsonists were ever apprehended. Until recently, under the strict investigation by Chief Detective Bai Naiduo, Russian Detective Bei Beining, Chinese Detective Feng Zhiming, Liu Shaoquan, Detectives Xie Futang, Zhang Fuquan, Yang Xiguang, etc. of the General Police Department, seven Russians were successively arrested on the 24th and 25th. It seemed that Ruodan was in the process of committing arson. Initially, Bin Liwei, a Russian in his sixties residing at 228 Hualong Road in the French Concession, purchased a large quantity of fox tails valued at about 450 yuan from the Pingjin area during the summer. He ostensibly consigned them to the Louise Moore Auction House for auction. On one hand, he colluded with accomplices to deliberately inflate the price before the auction to make goods valued at over 400 gold coins to be purchased at 6,000 yuan. At the time, the auction staff naturally did not suspect any ulterior motives, believing that the buyer must have a use for them, so they did not hesitate to spend heavily. In fact, Ruodan's purpose was to obtain a transaction price list given by Louise Moore. Immediately after obtaining this document, he turned to an insurance company to insure the goods according to the declared price. The insurance company, because the auction price of the goods was as high as 6,000 yuan, and their actual price should be more than 6,000 yuan, agreed to insure for 6,000 yuan. Ruodan then placed arson devices and various flammable liquids inside the cargo boxes, intending to store them at Longmao Foreign Firm's warehouse at 77 Guangdong Road on the 24th. Unexpectedly, his entire secret had been detected by Chinese and Western detectives. Therefore, on the morning of the 24th, they went together to the intersection of Lane 164, Long Road, which Ruodan had designated, to wait and watch. After waiting for a long time without any movement, they changed their location and went to Binli's place at 800 Xiafei Road. After waiting for a short time, they saw Bin Liwei coming. They followed him. In fact, he first entered 100 Shengmu Yuan Road for about an hour. Then, he went to 128 nearby to take out a large iron box and rode in a rickshaw to the back door of the residence of the Russian Keniler at 1228 Lafayette Road, placing the box at the door. He then took the original rickshaw to his residence at 228 Hualong Road, carried out a large hemp bag, and also transported it to the back door of Keniler's residence for temporary storage. Then he returned to his residence and carried out a rattan box. Later, Keniler transported these three boxes to the Longmao Foreign Firm's warehouse for storage. The Chinese and Western detectives who had been following all along arrested Keniler when he left the warehouse after finishing his business. At that time, Bin Liwei was waiting outside the warehouse door and was arrested at the same time. Subsequently, his accomplices Ao Peipan'er Sigan, Ma Jinggao Weisigan, Li Weisigan, Weisigan, Xi'er Xuhai were successively arrested at 6 Fanlong Road, Outside the Bund, 193 Xueshe Road, and a certain hotel in Ximo Road, 98 Hushan Road, etc. Items such as rubber tubes and empty bottles for liquids were found in each person's residence. The arson tools installed in the leather boxes containing fur were also taken out. Yesterday morning, including Bao Liwei and the other six, they were escorted to the First Special District Local Court, where Brigade Commander Qian Hongye conducted the preliminary interrogation. Ru Bao Yi, the lawyer representing the police department, briefly described the circumstances of the case, and requested an extension of the period for continued investigation, and then legally prosecuted after the conclusion of the investigation. Judge Qian then questioned the seven people one by one and ordered them to be detained for further interrogation at a later date.

Red Gao Slope Section of Jiujiang on the Shanghai-Hankou Line: Customs Has Prohibited Night Navigation; Downstream Vessels Prohibited from Sailing at Night; Upstream Vessels Should Stop to Give Way

The decreasing water volume of the Yangtze River and the increasing difficulty of navigation on the Shanghai-Hankou line have been reported in the newspapers. Yesterday, a reporter from Datong News Agency learned from the Jianghai Customs that night navigation has been prohibited for downstream vessels in the Honggaopo (Red High Slope) waterway of the Jiujiang section. The details are as follows:

Protecting Navigation Routes

The water levels along the downstream Shanghai to Hankou section continue to fall. The water level in Hankou has receded to within sixteen feet. The water levels at other ports such as Jiujiang, Anqing, and Wuhu are also decreasing daily, causing navigation to become increasingly dangerous in narrow channels and areas with rapid currents, especially for ships sailing downstream from Hankou to Shanghai. Therefore, in order to ensure the safety of navigation, the Customs will provide navigation methods at any time as the situation requires, to avoid collisions.

Night Navigation Prohibited

The Honggaopo waterway in the Jiujiang section is one such situation. Therefore, the Customs has prohibited night navigation for downstream vessels, except for half an hour before sunrise and half an hour after sunset, when downstream vessels are allowed to pass. When upstream vessels encounter downstream vessels in the waterway, they should absolutely stay to the right side of the channel, temporarily stop moving forward, and only start moving after the downstream vessels have passed. The Customs has strictly ordered all Yangtze River steamers to pay close attention to the above navigation methods.

Electrical Manufacturing Industry Submits to Railway Department: Request to Revise Flashlight Freight Rates; Exempt From Special Light and Bulky Goods List; Charge Fees as Usual to Maintain Domestic Goods

The Shanghai Electrical Manufacturing Industry Association submitted a report to the Ministry of Railways yesterday, stating that they are requesting the Ministry to quickly revise freight rates in order to maintain the transportation of domestic goods. According to a letter from the Huiming Battery Factory, a member of the association: "Regarding the new regulations on freight rates for light and bulky goods issued by the Ministry of Railways in Transportation Circular No. 8, flashlights are listed in the special light and bulky goods freight rate table, and fees are calculated by adding 50% to the actual weight. We believe that the new regulations have errors and hinder the sales of domestic goods. We should clarify this and request that the Ministry of Railways quickly reform the regulations to promote domestic goods. Our factory's production of Da Wuwei brand flashlights has been selling well in the provinces of Hebei, Shandong, Chahar, Suiyuan, Shanxi, Henan, and along the Beijing, Shanghai, Zhejiang, and Jiangxi lines. We have already received awards from the Ministry of Industry and the Shandong Provincial Construction Department, and the Ministry of Finance has granted us a tax exemption for exports. The annual production volume of these flashlights reaches more than 200,000 dozen, of which more than 90% are transported by rail. They are all packed in wooden boxes of 60 dozen each. The actual weight is 157 to 160 kilograms, and the volume is 68 cubic inches in height, 102 cubic inches in length, and 25 cubic inches in width, totaling 471 inches. The six-sided volume is 46. The combined weight is 157.216 kilograms. Before October 1st, the chargeable weight was 175 kilograms, which was not much different from the actual weight. Now they are listed in the special light and bulky goods list, and the calculation is based on adding 50% to the actual weight. This new regulation is actually flawed. According to the first provision of the new regulations on freight rates for light and bulky goods, 'Goods with a weight of one kilogram and a volume exceeding three cubic decimeters but not exceeding four cubic decimeters are considered ordinary light and bulky goods. Goods with a weight of one kilogram and a volume exceeding four cubic decimeters are considered special light and bulky goods.' The actual weight of our factory's flashlights is as described above, 157 to 160 kilograms per box. The calculated volume is 157.216 kilograms. In fact, the weight and volume are balanced and do not exceed the limit. Even if calculated according to 157 kilograms, the volume only exceeds 0.216 kilograms. If averaged per kilogram, the excess is even smaller. Even if calculated according to regulations, it should only be listed as ordinary light and bulky goods, with a fee calculated by adding 20% to the actual weight, and should not be listed in the special light and bulky goods list. In recent years, the flashlight industry has been facing the dumping of foreign goods and the threat of soaring raw material prices, while the selling price has been falling year by year due to weak purchasing power. They are struggling to survive in a precarious situation. Now that freight rates are affected again, costs are increasing, and sales are becoming more difficult. The interests of the future of the domestic goods industry are not superficial. Therefore, we have written this letter to explain our difficulties and request that you submit it to the Ministry of Railways to quickly reform the regulations and maintain the lifeline of the domestic goods industry." In response, we have submitted this report and earnestly request your Ministry to revise the freight rates for domestic flashlights, continue to charge fees as usual, and exempt them from being included in the special light and bulky goods category, in order to benefit the transportation of domestic goods, which would be a great favor.

Letters to the Editor

To the Editor:

We are writing to clarify that our association has decided that the interest rate for a six-month fixed deposit is 5.5 yuan per 1,000 yuan deposited for 30 days, which is equivalent to an annual interest rate of 6.6%. Today, your esteemed newspaper misinterpreted this as 5.5 yuan of interest per 1,000 yuan deposited for six months, which is equivalent to an annual interest rate of 1.1%. This does not correspond to the facts. Therefore, we are writing to request a correction. We hope you will investigate and correct this matter. Sincerely, Shanghai Money Industry Association, October 26, 1936.

To the Editor:

We are writing in response to the Shin Shi News Agency's news report in today's edition of your esteemed newspaper, which stated that Da Sheng Yarn Factory No. 1 is preparing to resume production. Our company's Factory No. 1 was established 40 years ago and has always been committed to improving domestic goods. Although the yarn industry has been in a slump for many years, we have continued to operate as usual. The report of the closure and resumption of production must be a rumor. We are writing to clarify this matter. We hope you will make a correction. Sincerely, Nantong Dasheng No. 1 Textile Company, February 26, 1936.

Reflections on Inspecting European Sports (Continued)

— Jiang Lianggui

(3) The Issue of Male Teachers Teaching Female Students

The so-called issue of male teachers teaching female students, 'Can male teachers teach female students or should they absolutely not?' When I was in China, I often heard high-sounding pronouncements from many women in the field of etiquette and education, and I saw many of their great works opposing male teachers teaching female students. Of course, we dare not say that they have any special purpose, but at least we think that they are somewhat acting rashly. Therefore, during this inspection, I paid close attention to this matter, and even wanted to take the opportunity to inquire about the situation in various European countries. Several female members of the inspection group raised the issue first. As a result, the answer each time was that in their countries, it is very common for men to teach female students, and most of the technical training is undertaken by men. When I was in Sweden, I specifically discussed this matter with my teacher, Mr. Zhang Huilan. As a result, we believed that men could teach female students, especially in technical aspects, which is easy to be effective, but in dance or gymnastics, women are more suitable. Originally, this was not a problem. The reasons why female comrades in China oppose male teachers teaching female students are:

A. Men do not understand the physiological conditions of female students.

B. Men cannot understand the psychology of female students.

In fact, these two reasons are untenable. As for the so-called physiological conditions, I think people who become physical education teachers certainly know them. The biggest difference between male and female physiology, apart from the difference in physical ability, is menstruation. Of course, during menstruation, female students are not suitable for strenuous activities except for very gentle activities. I think the so-called physiological condition of female students is this point. As for saying that female students are ashamed to inform male teachers of their periods, so male teachers cannot easily know, this situation may exist, but this kind of thinking is extremely wrong. Menstruation is a normal physiological phenomenon, and there is absolutely nothing to hide. For example, when the food in our stomach is completely digested, we feel hungry. This is the same phenomenon. When you are hungry, looking for food and menstruation are equally sacred things, so why hide it? As for psychology, I think it is a matter of people, not an entire factual problem. There are male teachers who do not understand the psychology of female students, and there are also female teachers who do not understand the psychology of female students.

(4) The Most Ideal Mass Sport

Today, the evaluation of sports activities in various European countries has reached a common and unanimous conclusion: After years of research, it is considered that the most beneficial for physical and mental health, and at the same time has educational, physiological, and military value, is swimming. Therefore, in several countries we have visited, such as Denmark, Germany, and Italy, swimming is designated as a compulsory course for schools at all levels. In the winter of 1935, the German Ministry of Education also issued the following decree: 'All elementary school students in the country must learn to swim. Those who do not know how to swim will not be allowed to graduate.' Germany is a country with compulsory education. Every citizen must go through a certain number of years of compulsory education. Therefore, it is planned that in ten years, all citizens born in 1925 will be able to swim. After this decree was issued, the government accelerated the training of a large number of swimming instructors to meet the urgent need. Denmark also has the same regulations. Although other countries do not have express regulations, they spare no effort to promote swimming. In Stockholm, Sweden, the government allocated a large amount of funds to train children to swim. Therefore, any city in various countries, no matter how big or small, has swimming pool buildings. At the same time, places with excellent natural environments, such as seashores and lakeside, are immediately set up with swimming pools. I have been to a small city in Germany called Marburg, with a population of only 20,000 people, and there are four swimming pools of various sizes, and there is also a warm water pool in winter. In fact, swimming is indeed 'the most ideal sport, and it is also economical. The daily consumption is extremely low, and it can also cultivate a kind of ability to cope with unexpected situations.' I hope that the sports bureaus and education bureaus of various cities in China will also formulate a ten-year plan, stipulate a kind of national game suitable for national conditions, no matter what kind of sport it is, as long as it meets the needs of the current Chinese situation, whether it is local or foreign, promote it as much as possible and implement it effectively. Doing this, I think, is more practical than spending millions of dollars to hold sports meetings. Fifteen years later, I dare to guarantee that the youth of the whole country will be able to become true new Chinese youth under a 'new model.'

(5) The Issue of the Transformation of Gymnastics Teaching Materials

(1) The Elimination of Footwork. Originally, this matter did not need to be mentioned again, but it has to be mentioned. As long as a few people who can think a little should understand that when attending physical education class, is it to ask students to specifically come one, two, one, march, or to ask them to spend a lot of energy to learn the changes in formations? This is extremely contrary to the principles of physical education. When I was in Shanghai, I visited the group gymnastics performance of the second Shanghai primary and secondary school sports meeting. What saddened me the most was that more than 90% of the schools still brought out that set of formation changes. Both teachers and students were extremely tired. I hope that the comrades who teach formation changes, let us think calmly, does this kind of one, two, one, marching teaching material have any effect on students? Does it have any impact? Undoubtedly, no one can answer. Then, this kind of teaching material is extremely unsuitable for children. Children are the life of the country. Our responsibility is to cultivate children. We must not mislead ourselves and others, and cause endless mistakes. During our visit, we visited several schools' physical education classes and never saw any teaching materials that used footwork. The most common thing is to do preparatory activities at the beginning of physical education class, using running. The types of running are different, and the methods are the same, but they can be fast or slow or changed to avoid being monotonous and lacking interest. After running, each sport begins.

(2) The Use of Music. Gymnastics and music are indeed very relevant, especially in girls and primary and secondary schools, because the harmonious rhythm of music, the ups and downs of tones, and the pleasant sounds of the piano all stimulate students' interest and reduce fatigue during exercise. In this regard, Europe has made the most of it.

(6) Youth Training and Children's Army

Youth training is one of the most important policies in various European countries, especially in Italy and Germany. The youth of the whole country, from childhood to adulthood, are given strict protection and guidance in terms of intellectual spirit, thought, and physical fitness, so that they become the most perfect citizens when they reach adulthood. In China, I think this is also an extremely important task. The biggest crisis in China at present is the decline of youth's physical fitness and the lack of knowledge. When China wants to implement this, it does not need to start a new organization, but can reform and expand the scope from the existing Chinese Practical Children's Army, not limited to students being able to join. All children of a certain age must join. Regarding this issue, I plan to write a more detailed and specific plan in the near future and discuss it with comrades.

Written in a rambling manner, the thoughts are not organized, and the text is not revised. Moreover, with a tube to spy on a leopard, what I see cannot be far away. I hope that the advanced people in China will give me corrections. I have too many feelings about this European tour. At the same time, every issue cannot be finished in a short time. In the future, when I have free time after class, I will slowly study with comrades. (September 30, 25th year, Berlin)

Zhejiang Literature Exhibition to Open Soon: Exhibits from Beijing, Shanghai, and Suzhou Arrived Yesterday and Are Being Actively Arranged; Opening Ceremony on October 31st, Open to the Public the Next Day

The Zhejiang Literature Exhibition has been preparing for several months and has been scheduled to open on November 1st at the Zhejiang Provincial Library in Hangzhou. It is now known that the executive committee of the association will have a number of design committee members and guests from all walks of life attending the opening ceremony, and it is expected that many will come from Beijing and Shanghai. In order to make the opening ceremony grand and to facilitate the design committee members and guests to carefully visit the exhibition, the opening ceremony has been advanced by one day to 9:00 am on October 31st at the Provincial Library on Daxue Road. At that time, Director Xu Shaodi of the Department of Education will personally preside over the ceremony and will invite a respected elder from the province to unveil the curtain. Recently, invitations have been sent to design committee members and representatives of various agencies in and out of the province to participate. It is heard that Mr. Zhang Jusheng, Ye Yuhu, Zhang Yongni of Shanghai, and Pan Boshan, Qu Bogang of Suzhou, are all scheduled to go to Hangzhou to participate. On the day of the ceremony, a tour of the exhibition venue will be led for the design committee members and guests, with the aim of further improving the layout based on collective opinions. The next day, November 1st, will be the start of the public exhibition, which is scheduled to last for half a month until the 15th. The association has received exhibits from various places inside and outside the province. In addition to the 50+ counties (all belonging to the former 11 prefectures) within the province that should have been requested, there are also public and private collectors from Shanghai, Nanjing, Beiping, Hankou, Wuxi, Suzhou, Jinan, and other places. The most numerous exhibits are from Shanghai and Suzhou. The association specially sent the collection director Yu Wangyao to Beijing and then to Suzhou and Shanghai to visit the collectors. A total of more than 200 items collected by the Shanghai collection branch before the event and newly collected from collectors were transported to Hangzhou yesterday (the 25th). Those that have been mailed and those that are planned to be brought to Hangzhou before the event are not included. The exhibits from within the province were transported to Hangzhou a few days ago, including a large number of cultural relics from the Wenzhou area. The Ningbo Tianyige and other cultural relics will arrive within three days. As of today, a total of more than 6,000 books, calligraphy, rubbings, antiques, etc. have been received from various parties. The Provincial Library has been working day and night in separate groups since this week, engaging in registration, verification, and preparing description cards. The reading room and part of the second floor are planned to be used as the exhibition venue, and they are currently being actively arranged. In order to better protect the calligraphy and paintings and rare books from damage, the association has specially invited Mr. Sun Yituo, who has extensive experience in ancient books, to be responsible for the unrolling and rolling work of the calligraphy and paintings and handscrolls during the layout, and has entrusted Mr. Zhu Suixiang to introduce people to assist in the layout. In addition, strict storage regulations and visiting rules have been formulated during the exhibition period, and the Public Security Bureau has sent senior police officers to be stationed in the library to avoid negligence.

Twenty-Fourth Year Financial Overview of Yenching University

Needs Approximately 900,000 Yuan

Yenching University has released its financial overview for the twenty-fourth year as follows:

The school’s income and expenditure final accounts for the twenty-fourth year have been audited and finalized by Thomson & Co. The complete report comprises more than forty tables, the contents of which are complex and difficult to grasp without detailed review. In order to make it clear for those who care about the school and easy to reference, a summary report has been compiled as follows. Although the school’s annual operating expenses have been streamlined and economized as much as possible over the past few years, it still requires approximately 900,000 yuan in national currency per year. Less than half of this amount comes from reliable, fixed sources. The majority is from temporary donations and subsidies from various parties. 1. The total revenue for the entire twenty-fourth year was 900,697.92 yuan in national currency. The sources are as follows: (1) Appropriation from the New York Board of Trustees, equivalent to 398,874.03 yuan in national currency, accounting for 44% of the total. (2) Subsidy from the Ministry of Education, 63,048.60 yuan, accounting for 7%. (3) Subsidy from the Rockefeller Foundation, 102,325.00 yuan, accounting for 11%. (4) Assistance from the China Foundation for the Promotion of Education and Culture, 15,000.00 yuan, accounting for 2%. (5) Fees paid by students, 136,134.4 yuan, accounting for 15%. (6) Assistance from various Christian mission boards, 67,200.00 yuan, accounting for 8%. (7) Other income, 124,396.78 yuan, accounting for 13%. 2. The total expenditure for the entire twenty-fourth year was 871,432.68 yuan, allocated as follows: (1) Administrative expenses, 149,232.39 yuan, accounting for 17%. (2) Building maintenance expenses, 88,741.82 yuan, accounting for 10%. (3) School of Religion, 21,024.02 yuan, accounting for 2%. (4) College of Arts, 196,825.70 yuan, accounting for 23%. (5) College of Science, 151,311.61 yuan, accounting for 17%. (6) College of Law, 111,541.23 yuan, accounting for 13%. (7) Graduate Institute of Sinology, 104,585.97 yuan, accounting for 12%. (8) Other, 84,169.94 yuan, accounting for 6%. The surplus after offsetting income and expenditure is 35,546.24 yuan. This surplus is due to the fact that when preparing the budget for this year, the exchange rate between US dollars and national currency was assumed to be 1:2.25. After the National Government implemented the new currency policy in November of last year, the price of US dollars rose to over 3.3 yuan. Therefore, from November onwards, the school received over one yuan in legal tender for each US dollar compared to the budgeted figure, resulting in this unexpected surplus at the end of the year. This sum has now been separately deposited and used as a reserve for future exchange rate gains and losses.

Unified Youth Cultivation (Part 1)

— Ying Guan

(Educational Broadcast on September 8th)

Everyone realizes that middle school students today bear too heavy a learning burden. They are already overwhelmed with academic subjects, and they also have to practice various sports and exercises, participate in extracurricular activities, engage in labor service, attend large camps and grand reviews, etc. New tricks emerge endlessly, almost to the point of making a young person dizzy, exhausted, and hoarse, and yet it's still not over. This is the need of education in this era; lacking any one of these is unacceptable. However, is this truly the purpose of education?

No one can deny that today's youth are the future masters of the country. Because our nation has encountered unprecedented misfortune, the historical mission that we, on behalf of the people, bear for the nation is also unprecedentedly arduous. However, the age of junior high school students is still within childhood, and high school is only the early stage of youth. Their bodies and minds are developing and are very fragile, unable to withstand heavy workloads. Bearing arduous missions is a matter for the future, not something that can be immediately undertaken. Precisely because the future responsibility is great, current care for their physical and mental development should be even more meticulous. We absolutely cannot immediately push the ruined affairs of the nation, which predecessors and ourselves have messed up, entirely onto the youth, as if the debts owed by the elders and ourselves are immediately pushed onto the underage children, demanding that they repay them immediately. Where in the world is there such a ridiculous thing?

When youth encounter this time of inheriting great burdens and undertaking difficult tasks, amidst the complicated responsibilities, they should establish a unified method for cultivating knowledge, physique, and character in order to grasp the key points, handle them succinctly, and avoid being exhausted in coping and worn out in rushing around. This unified cultivation method can be divided into several aspects. First, the administrative organs in charge of education and all organizations responsible for leading youth often complain that the central government's decrees for youth education and training from various high-level competent authorities often conflict, making them difficult to comply with. To my knowledge, this situation has recently been addressed by close liaison between the central government's high-level competent authorities, striving to avoid duplication and contradiction in decrees. In the future, the local competent authorities responsible for youth education and training can also negotiate and establish effective liaison methods to ensure that the central government's unified decrees can be implemented thoroughly. At the same time, the local competent authorities should no longer have methods that conflict with central laws and regulations. Naturally, there are times when central laws and regulations need local supplementation, but the supplementation should not contain conflicting meanings. In short, all competent authorities should pay attention to the total amount of burden on the youth, that is, the daily working time and the amount of energy that an average young person should have. Before issuing any laws and regulations that increase the learning burden on youth, they should consider whether the time and energy of the youth can bear it. They cannot treat the youth as county magistrates in the administrative organization, where all upper-level authorities issue empty decrees demanding that the county comply, and the county magistrate deserves to die ten thousand times. If they were to comply with each and every decree, they truly would not be able to handle it and would have to ignore them all altogether. To be blunt, the youth do not have the rich experience of the county magistrates and do not know how to perfunctorily carry out orders. If you tell them to do this and that, they will truly do it, working themselves to exhaustion, both physically and mentally, without time to consider anything else.

Second, school administrative structures. Schools are the only important link between competent authorities at all levels and the youth. Their position can either improve or worsen the implementation of the upper-level authorities' decrees. In the past, most secondary schools were often ineffective in implementing laws and regulations, maintaining an attitude of seeking nothing but avoiding blame, perfunctorily dealing with matters. As a result of the rectification over the past few years, this phenomenon has undergone a complete reversal, that is, most schools have become somewhat eager for quick success. Regardless of the orders from any quarter, they immediately put them into operation without hesitation. As for whether various methods conflict, whether certain methods are useless or harmful, and how excessive or what the results of the implementation are, they have no time to consider. Only in this way is it considered diligence, in order to please everyone and even deliberately seek praise. They do not make practical efforts in the fundamental training of youth but think up scattered, diverse methods on the surface to drive youth into activity. In this way, to outsiders, not only is the implementation of laws and regulations considered effective, but there are also extra achievements. What honor this is! Pitifully, how many innocent youth are destroyed and sacrificed under this honor is unknown.

The situation described above is still the problem committed by some schools that want to please everyone and deliberately seek quick success. Now, let's cite a common malpractice that is easily committed by general schools. For example, physical education should naturally be compulsory and require all students to participate. However, the health of each young person should still be taken into account. If the body has a certain defect, certain sports should be exempted or a certain corrective exercise should be administered, or if the student is temporarily suffering from a certain disease, the entire or part of the sports should be temporarily suspended. These should all be closely monitored at all times. Active exercise is beyond reproach, but preventing abuses and oversights cannot be condoned. Facts tell us that many youth have contracted various serious diseases such as nephritis, scarlet fever, acute pneumonia, etc., due to participation in Boy Scout reviews, camping, and snow driving, before and after which the school neglected prevention. There are also many young people who have already suffered from serious illnesses such as heart failure, pulmonary tuberculosis, etc., but the authorities neglect to notice and still order them to continue participating in military training, resulting in death. In this case, the instructors and officers are naturally difficult to escape the blame, but even more to blame are the school administrators and the responsible personnel in charge of military training. Due to the disastrous defeat of our country's athletes in the recent World Games, it is inevitable that school sports must be stepped up in the future. At the same time, the occurrence of various dangers and diseases will also gradually increase. How to prevent and deal with them should be one of the special matters that school administration should pay special attention to in the future. Do not sacrifice a number of outstanding young people who can be accomplished in fields other than sports for nothing before there is any certainty of achieving scores in the next World Games.

In short, an enlightened secondary school principal and a sound school administrative structure should naturally implement the decrees of the upper-level authorities in a practical manner. At the same time, they should still not forget the broad goals of youth education and youth training, use their own thinking, and aim to maximize the benefits of implementation, reduce possible drawbacks to the lowest limit, not act perfunctorily, not eagerly seek fame, but actively and thoughtfully strive forward.

Third, the youth themselves. What has been said above is addressed to the various competent authorities and school administrative structures that educate and train the youth. Because in order to achieve unified youth cultivation, it is impossible to hope that the various competent authorities and schools will first have a unified training method. Although it is an external article, it is also the preface to this article. What follows will talk about the youth themselves, which can be said to be the main text of unified youth cultivation. It can also be divided into three levels. (To be continued)

Western Boys' School to Set Up Russian Class

The Education Committee of the Shanghai Municipal Council, at the request of the Russian community in the city, has proposed to the Council that a Russian class be established in the Western Boys' School of the Shanghai Municipal Council to teach Russian children. The education of Western children in the city, Russian children are the most neglected. There is only one extremely small Russian children's school in the city. The addition of a Russian class may provide some remedy. The Council has approved this proposal, but the continuation, expansion, or termination of this plan will depend on its success.

Tien Chu Prize Essay Contest

Mao Hongjun Wins Second Prize, Wang Weizu Wins Third Prize

The results of the first and second "Tien Chu Prize" essay contests of the Chinese Chemical Industry Society this year have been determined. The winners are Mao Hongjun for "A Glimpse of the Swedish Paper Industry" (Second Prize) and Wang Weizu for "A Glimpse of the Japanese Chemical Industry" (Third Prize). Wan Darong's "Research on the Manufacture of Indanthrene Blue and its Derivative Dyes" and "Research on the Manufacture of BO Indanthrene Deep Blue and its Derivative Dyes," Hua Guoxiang's "Research on the Manufacture of Activated Carbon," and Xu Xieming's "Chalk Industry" are all deemed qualified and receive remuneration. The essays will be published in the Society's journal "Chemical Industry," Volumes 11 and 12. The fourth essay contest of the year will close at the end of December. The rules are as follows: (1) Prizes: First Prize 100 yuan, Second Prize 60 yuan, Third Prize 40 yuan. (2) Frequency: Four times a year, closing at the end of March, June, September, and December. (3) Scope: Theoretical research and practical investigation of chemical industry. (4) Publication: The selected essays will be published in the Society's journal "Chemical Industry." (5) Detailed regulations: The regulations for the "Tien Chu Prize" essay contest can be obtained from the Society at 381 Bubbling Well Road, Shanghai.

Guo Hua Middle School Invites Xu Xingchu to Give a Lecture

Guo Hua Middle School held its eighth memorial week gathering yesterday. Students gathered in the auditorium, sang the party song, and respectfully read the will. Xu Xingchu, who had just returned from Italy, was invited to give a lecture. He said that Italy's new education places the greatest emphasis on middle schools, believing that a good foundation laid in middle school will enable students to cope with society in the future. Middle school students are absolutely disciplined, respect teachers, and never interfere in school administration. Compared to today's students in our country, there is a world of difference. He sincerely hoped that our young people would follow this as a model, which would be fortunate for the future of education in our country. It is said that the playwright Ouyang Yuqian has been scheduled to give a lecture next week.

This month is the final act of the yarn market, with various parties determined to take delivery. There were rumors of a deal at 240 yuan. Unexpectedly, prices stagnated after being too high. There are still many people who sell short when prices rise.

The price of 16-pound five-fu double elephant coarse cloth fell (per piece) by 4 jiao, the price of 14-pound blue chicken single deer fell (per piece) by 5 jiao, the price of 13-pound nine-day flying bear three horses fell (per piece) by 3 jiao, the price of 10-pound three rabbits, three deer, and three cats fell (per piece) by 1 jiao, the price of 9-pound five-fu cat eagle fell (per piece) by 3 jiao and a half. The factory's coarse cloth is mostly lacking stalls.
