Shen Bao Local Supplement

Discussion

The Key to Breaking Through the Difficulties Lies in Japan

— Me

Since Japanese Ambassador Kawagoe came to China and had his first negotiation with Foreign Minister Zhang, even if the conditions have been slightly flexible, the opinions have never been close. Therefore, the news reports on the Sino-Japanese negotiations have recently revealed that sometimes the atmosphere is tense, and sometimes the situation is relaxed. In fact, since the Kawagoe-Zhang negotiations, there has never been any relaxation, and there has never been any optimism. The so-called relaxation is just some diplomatic air, not the truth.

May I ask, has the other party's established policy changed? Has the policy of aggression been abandoned? At most, it is just a matter of degree, so where does the relaxation come from? Where does the peace come from? The Japanese policy of aggression against China was originally one, but it was carried out either through diplomatic channels or not. Therefore, if the Japanese established policy remains unchanged, whether it is through diplomatic channels or not, this road will always be blocked.

Therefore, now, if we want to see how tense or relaxed the situation in the Sino-Japanese negotiations is, we should first look at the other party's actions in North China. There is no need to talk about anything else. Even arbitrarily building airfields, arbitrarily increasing troops stationed, arbitrarily conducting large-scale exercises, arbitrarily protecting smuggling, and arbitrarily investing in the development of North China, are these all relaxed attitudes? One side is in the process of mediation, while the other side has not slightly withdrawn its traces of aggression. May I ask, where does the relaxation come from?

Moreover, looking at the recent Japanese newspaper editorials, their attitudes are very inconsistent. Most of them advocate proceeding through diplomatic channels, while another group of newspapers has quite radical editorials. Although the attitudes of both sides are different in terms of soft and hard, and rigidity and flexibility, one wants to achieve its goal by using gentle methods, and the other wants to achieve its goal by using radical methods. Although the methods used by both sides are different, they actually have the same goal by different routes.

If those who advocate solving the problem through diplomatic channels can abandon their original consistent advocacy and truly implement the principle of goodwill, it would certainly be welcome to us. If, however, they proceed through diplomatic channels but still adhere to their consistent policy, then it is better to be radical and lose national sovereignty and territory than to be gentle and lose national sovereignty and territory. The iron case is as solid as a mountain and cannot be shaken. For this diplomatic negotiation, no matter how difficult it is and no matter how many twists and turns there are, there is absolutely no room for compromise outside of not losing an iota of sovereignty over the territory of North China. This is indeed the consensus of all the people of our country, and it is also what the government authorities have sworn to and can be questioned by heaven and earth.

Therefore, whether the difficulties of this negotiation can be broken through depends entirely on Japan, not on our country. Our country's minimum demands have absolutely no flexibility or borrowing; only by studying the soft and hard tones of foreign newspapers, there are also two types of natures. One is to simply make these two tones, the so-called intimidation and inducement, combining both soft and hard, so that our country is easy to comply. This is indeed a kind of diplomatic tactic. One is that Japanese diplomacy towards China was originally divided into two factions, one advocating relaxation and one advocating radicalism. The opinions of the two factions were originally incompatible. The contradiction within itself is prone to internal disputes. This is the so-called Hirota himself standing at a crossroads. We now do not ask whether it is a tactic or a divergence. We must set our minds, insist on territorial sovereignty, and not give up even an iota. Our country can ignore whether the tactics are hard or soft.

Punishment

— Lyon

When I was a child, I loved to listen to Broad-Mouth Zhang San tell stories about "beheadings." I was often both happy and scared. I was happy because he gesticulated and told the stories vividly. I was scared because he told them so realistically that it seemed like there was a killing field in front of me. The "wooden stump" rolling under the eaves seemed like a head that had just been cut off, and it even seemed to be flashing its eyes. The more I listened, the more scared I became, but the more scared I was, the more I wanted to listen. This is exactly like the saying "Knowing there are tigers in the mountains, I prefer to go to the tiger mountains." Perhaps children's psychology is naturally like this. The most touching part of what Broad-Mouth Zhang San said was, "No sooner said than done, the knife rose and a head fell, blood spurted out, everyone clapped their hands, and some people dipped steamed buns in the hot blood to eat..."

Such scary situations would often fall into my dreams, and I would jump straight out of bed in a panic. My mother found out the reason and forbade me to go to the ancestral hall and hang out with Broad-Mouth Zhang San. Later, I don't know how, Broad-Mouth Zhang San stole the incense burner and candle holder from the ancestral hall. The clan chief ordered someone to break his right leg and drive him out of the village. That day, I happened to be sending cotton strips to my aunt's house. I don't know how such an interesting person endured that physical punishment.

Until now, I have never seen a public execution. One reason is the lack of opportunity, and the other is that my mood is not as good as it was in childhood. I often can't bear to watch the killing of chickens or the gutting of fish. The bright, shiny blade, the tearing of the thin skin and flesh, and the splashing of blood can all give me a strong feeling of cruelty. Although I don't have that shallow "compassion," I did refuse a friend's invitation to visit a "cattle slaughtering company." I am really afraid of the execution ground for the cattle. Because I was accidentally pricked by a steel needle and my finger hurt all night, it made me think of blades, ropes, lead bullets, "skinning machines," electric chairs... all kinds of scientific and historical instruments of torture for dealing with people or things, and the cruelty and pain of physical punishment that is better than "needle pricking fingers."

But the more I want to avoid something, the more I can't avoid it. The mutton shop at the entrance of the alley is opening again in due season. Usually, whenever I see a pig's head hanging on the iron hook in the butcher shop, with the severed neck oozing blood, I seem to feel a slight pain in my own neck. This must be a nervous reaction. What's more, the mutton shop is killing sheep in public at the door, scalding them with boiling water, plucking their wool, breaking their bellies, splitting their heads, and putting them in steaming barrels. In general, this kind of situation is considered extremely ordinary. Some "eaters" will even show a leisurely attitude, assessing that the "water content" of the sheep that is being pressed on the long bench by the butcher and waiting to be slaughtered is not bad, and some people are waiting halfway to buy sheep's blood or sheep's wool. I really admire them. After all, their hearts are several times stronger than mine. They have no qualms about the death sentence being suffered by living things. In their minds, except for "eating pleasure" and "profit," there is no premonition of anything else. Or the biggest reason is that the one who is dying is not of the same kind?

However, isn't the world full of crowds of people like sheep who are being slaughtered by their own kind? But they also show a leisurely attitude, harboring "profit" calculations, holding a "eating pleasure" principle, and waiting for opportunities halfway. This not only makes me admire, but it simply makes me amazed.

Because I have to pass through the alley every day, I have many opportunities to see the scene of killing sheep at the entrance of the mutton shop. It is almost the same as listening to Broad-Mouth Zhang San tell "beheading" stories. The more scared I am, the more unbearable it is, but the more I want to take a look. This temporary psychological abnormality often takes precedence. Several times I stood in the crowd of idlers watching the killing of sheep. At first, the sheep were very docile and were thrown on the long bench. The butcher grabbed the skin and flesh between its head and neck, and the sharp knife pierced through it. With a cry of "Ma," fresh blood gushed out from the severed throat and poured into the bucket. When I looked at the remaining two sheep tied to the pillars, they were already wandering around, but they had lost their freedom to survive.

When the second one was started, it actually started a kind of stubborn and struggling action. However, torture was finally added to it by the butcher's smirk. At this time, I thought: If I were that third sheep, seeing two companions being killed one after another, how sad and indignant would I be, and how would I free myself from the imminent torture. However, sheep are finally sheep, and the "fat" and "docility" of sheep have only created "eating pleasure" and "profit" for ordinary people. Just like me, who is thin and often fights with fate, I have to endure the whip of a cow for a living. This is a kind of vicious "private punishment." However, am I so docile?

At the Tomb

— Li Liwen

The warm morning sun makes one feel a bit lazy. Dewdrops shimmer between the blades of grass. Something rustles gently and softly. The grass, the green expanse, breathes shallowly, emitting a rich fragrance. Several sparrows hop on the bamboo fence, while diligent farmers are already tilling the fields, the hoes flashing in the sunlight.

I followed that cinder path, turned several bends, and entered the cemetery—finding the place from yesterday.

Everything was still the same as yesterday: two baskets of flowers placed on the tombstone, dewdrops clinging to the flowers.

I sat down.

It is said that a wanderer is good at dreaming, reminiscing—and feeling melancholic.

I sat there. Something slipped into my mind, making me restless. For a time, many thoughts about the past, the future—uncontrollable tides of thought—surged up. ...

I thought of the stubborn old man, thought of my own wandering life.

I sighed deeply. I never dreamed that one day I would be able to personally watch the person I admired most enter the earth, nor did I expect that, although I had no chance to meet him while he was alive, this stubborn person now lived so close to my residence—or could even be said to be my neighbor.

In this complex and contradictory mood, I deeply tasted the irreplaceable sorrow, but at the same time, I began to console myself with an Ah Q-like selfishness.

For many years, often when I was in trouble in Java, searching for work from one town to another, when I begged for travel expenses to cross the Java Sea to the lush, malaria-infested Borneo and suffered my brother-in-law's cold shoulder, when I stayed in a hotel on Changdi Er Malu in Guangzhou for more than a month and was finally driven out, or even—when my family finally took pity and sent money to support me to embark on the proud student life I am now living, I had a burning desire to pour out my feelings. However, to whom should I pour them out? In the vast sea of people, I could hardly find anyone!—I never dreamed that this stubborn old man, whom I had admired since my childhood in the first year of junior high school, would one day lie in a place I could reach. Now, I have finally found a place to pour out my feelings. Regardless of whether this stubborn old man is lying silently in the grave, regardless of

Page 18

whether this stubborn old man can hear me or not, I have finally found a place to pour out my feelings. From now on, I plan to come here whenever I have a chance, to keep the old man company and pour out the words I have wanted to say for years. This old man, who was so stubborn in life that he struggled with the disease for ten years even after microbes had eroded his lungs, I believe he is just as stubborn after death—perhaps, he can hear my outpouring, and that would be my satisfaction!

The cemetery worker walked by, casting a strange glance at me.

"There's still work to be done; this tomb isn't finished yet!" he said.

I nodded to him, thanking him for his concern.

The stone mason by the roadside outside the cemetery's bamboo fence began to work with a clanging sound.

Chronicles of Jin River Bay

— Yegao

Jin River Chronicle 4

The boat had arrived at Jin River Bay, not far from our destination. Here, we would have a half-day stopover, because everything we had stored for eating and using was almost gone.

In front of the bay was a small market, formed by several interconnected large villages, with two short and quiet streets running back and forth. More than a hundred earthen-tile houses were lazily crowded on both sides, low, dilapidated, and filled with a desolate feeling. Half a year ago, this was a bustling place with a population of 30,000. Rice mills, large businesses, money houses, the export of inland local products, and the import of foreign goods all passed through here. But since the last time they "ge" something, the situation has changed. The wealthy families have rolled up the essence of the entire market and fled. Now, what remains is just the dregs and husks of this market!

After the boat docked, the boatman carried a large bag ashore to buy rice and vegetables. We stayed in the cabin to watch over things. Sometimes, feeling stuffy, we would climb out of the cabin and stand on the deck, glancing at the shore. Perhaps it was because our attire was a bit different from the locals, but we immediately attracted the attention of the people coming and going on the shore. The slope of the pier was crowded with about twenty or thirty idle people, all so thin and ragged. In such cold days, there were even people living half-naked.

We stood for a while, afraid that gathering too many people on the shore would cause trouble, so we waved our hands to them and wanted to climb back into the cabin. Unexpectedly, this made them burst into loud laughter, and the sound still echoed brightly in the air even after we had settled in the cabin.

After about a quarter of an hour, the sound had subsided. We tentatively climbed out of the cabin again. The curious people had dispersed, and the pier was quiet. However, not far from us, there were already two people, sneaking onto a small barge docked by the shore, climbing towards our boat.

One of these two people was an old man of about fifty years old, short and thin, with a sallow face. He was wearing a half-naked garment full of patches. Closely following behind him was a girl of fourteen or fifteen years old, with her hair cut short and scattered loosely on her head, her face thin, dark, and petite. She was wearing a large garment that did not match her figure at all. Her two bare feet nimbly searched every plank, jumping from here to there.

This aroused our curiosity, so we watched them carefully. However, they stood motionless on a broken stern plank adjacent to our boat. The old man's face showed a worried and hesitant look. The little girl hid half behind him, shyly biting her hem, her face lowered, looking at her pair of withered little bare feet. The old man looked at us for a while, then suddenly said softly to the little girl:

"Go ahead, don't be shy, they are good guests. ..."

After saying that, he shook the little girl's shoulders, turned around, and walked back towards the shore. The little girl looked at us timidly with doubtful eyes, then suddenly jumped nimbly onto our boat, her thin lips trembling slightly.

"What's the matter?" We called out to her with some confusion, with a stern look on our faces. She probably didn't expect us to be like this, and hurriedly took two steps back in surprise, clutching her head tightly with both hands, as if afraid we would hit her. She turned her head back to look at the shore. On the shore, the old man was standing anxiously, waving his hand at her angrily:

"Little devil! What are you afraid of? They are good guests. ..."

She looked helpless, then turned back to us again. Suddenly, in her deep eye sockets, several crystal tears welled up, and she sobbed softly in a breathless voice.

"What do you want?" we asked her again, but our tone was already gentle.

"... Sirs, save the poor... give me some money, I'll sleep with you... " she wiped away her tears with her hand, her voice trembling, her face covered with a deep blush. "We are starving. There is no way. ..." After saying that, she cried again, sobbing.

We looked at each other, and we understood everything. What made this immature girl do such a lowly thing? It was hunger. Although we knew that this hunger threatened more than just her here, that tens of thousands of people were living like her, a strong sense of sympathy made us unable to help but give her some help. We searched our bodies for the few foreign coins we had and gave them to her. She held them in her hands as if she had obtained a treasure, and turned back to the shore. The old man's face was shining with light, and he hurriedly shouted loudly again:

"Kowtow to the sirs!"

But we stopped her and waved our hands to tell her to go. She hesitated, then turned and walked away.

A Daughter of Penang

— Harris

Taking a ship all night from the remote port where I grew up, I arrived at the docks of Penang in the clear morning as the sky barely dawned and the light radiated everywhere. Before coming, I had already sent a letter to my aunt who lives here, so this morning, my cousin specially took half a day off from the foreign firm he works for and waited for me at the dock with a smile. I had not seen my cousin for two years, and he had matured a lot—As we rode in the car towards my aunt's house, I also asked about my cousin, Irene.

"Ah, Irene?" A look of joy appeared on my cousin's face, "She is already a beautiful girl."

Sure enough, in the living room of my aunt's house, I met Irene—a slender figure, wearing a thin white gauze western dress, but with a pair of embroidered slippers on her feet, obviously she was at home and not going out. The shallow dimples still remained at the corners of her mouth, but her skin was darker than before. Besides, even her hair was no different from when we met two years ago. In this first meeting, my aunt was too talkative, asking about the situation at home and my mother's health, until it was almost time to eat, and Irene did not interrupt a single word, sitting on the side, holding a novel and reading. It wasn't until after dinner, when my aunt went back to her room to rest, that I had a chance to talk to Irene.

"Irene, you've grown so much!" I began like this.

"Really!" she replied, lowering her head, as if she wasn't as innocent and mischievous as usual.

"We haven't seen each other for two years, so we're a bit estranged... Irene, I'm so happy to have my father's permission to come to Penang to study! I thought that we could live together in the future, and see each other every day, and I was so happy..."

I said, staring straight at her. At this time, she raised her head as if she had been touched by something, her eyes met mine, and then she said to me:

"You are so lucky. But I can't continue studying."

"What? Did you say you're not going to study?" I asked anxiously.

"It's not that I don't love to continue studying, but it's my father and mother's idea. They think that once a daughter reaches seventeen or eighteen, she shouldn't show her face outside anymore! She has to hide at home, waiting to get married..."

"Is there such a thing? What era is this!" I exclaimed indignantly.

But my indignation did not get my aunt's understanding. When I protested to her on behalf of my cousin Irene, she replied with a smile: "You are really an ignorant child!" Outside, I met several educators from Penang, and they told me that Penang is the place where China's inherent feudal ideas are the strongest; no one sympathizes with the oppression that daughters suffer. They also said that women's education is more popular anywhere in the Malay Peninsula, but only in Penang is it murky.

Irene seemed to just listen to the dictates of fate regarding her future and did not participate in her own opinions at all—this is such a mistake! The summer vacation was about to pass, and the schools were busy with the approaching start of the school term, and I also registered at a middle school. Irene, on the other hand, was still hiding at home reading novels, spending her bleak days. I really couldn't stand it anymore. One day, I grabbed her and said:

"Irene, listen to me for a few words. What's the difference between a girl and a boy? She should enjoy the right to live like a boy, and receive the same education! If you listen to the words of your stubborn old father, then you are just a slave. Where is your freedom, and where is your happiness? Irene, go to school. If Penang can't allow you to do this, can't you return to the motherland? Your brother will give you financial help, I talked to him about it this morning."

After hearing me say this in one breath, Irene threw the book aside as if she was very moved, and asked:

"Really? Can brother really do it?"

"You can ask him yourself."

My cousin promised everything, and this Irene, who was originally as docile as a lamb, suddenly stirred up a rebellious mood. One morning when it was drizzling, just as the sky was dawning, Irene carried simple luggage, escorted by me and my cousin, to the pier, leaving a letter to her parents at home. On the way to the pier, Irene shouted with rare excitement:

"Old Penang, goodbye! Really goodbye!"

It was drizzling, drizzling! When we got to the pier, it was raining even harder, as if it wanted to wash Penang completely, making people feel extra happy.

As the ship's whistle blew, Irene stood on the deck and waved to us. She must still be shouting in her heart:

"Really goodbye, old Penang!"

Ah Q

Lu Xun is dead! We have nothing to commemorate him with, so all members of our society will from today onwards broadcast Ah Q to comfort his departed soul.

Although the script is not from his pen, in any case, Mr. Chen Mengshao adapted it based on the True Story.

Ah Q is a representative figure of the proletariat and the ignorant class. Those who know Ah Q say he is a loyal worker, those who do not know Ah Q say he is a thieving rogue. Those who know Ah Q say he is a solitary person with "humanity," those who do not know Ah Q say he is an obscene thing. Those who know Ah Q say he is a plaintiff of human grievance, those who do not know Ah Q say he is a damnable traitor.

Ah Q's character brought to people is the extreme portrayal of the inferior nature of the Chinese people. Mr. Lu Xun's creation of the True Story of Ah Q shocked the literary world, naturally our current era will absolutely not allow the existence of Ah Q, but we hope that the Ah Q attitude of the Chinese people will end here, because the current situation requires us to wash away the shame of Ah Q!

Storytelling with Musical Accompaniment

Cao Xiaoying's Yu Qing Ting

Central-Western (1040) 1:00 PM to 1:45 PM

Opening: "Shepherd's Scroll"

Crushing the bandits, he returned home in glory. Zhu Chundeng returned to his hometown with an imperial decree. But alas, he did not see his loving mother and wife. He hurriedly asked his aunt about their whereabouts. The wolf-hearted woman had a glib tongue, saying that the mother and daughter-in-law had gone to the afterlife. Hearing this was like a thunderbolt. He cried so hard his heart was breaking. He held a funeral and helped the poor, doing good deeds to pray for the deceased. But who knew that the mother and daughter-in-law were still alive, suffering family disasters and hiding in the deep mountains. They lived with a shepherd among the sheep, longing for their family but not daring to return. They endured hardship and begged for food, filled with tears and grief. Husband and wife met at the tomb, and they were surprised by each other's appearance. After questioning each other, the truth came out. Only then did they know that the aunt's conscience was lost, and his dear mother had cried her eyes dry. They changed into official robes on the spot, their suffering came to an end, and they smiled. The evil woman was anxious at this time, kneeling in the middle and vowing to clear suspicion. But unexpectedly, before the vow was finished, a blue dragon arrived, and her bones turned to ashes in an instant. Her own wickedness could not be avoided.

Chen Lianqing and Qi Lianfang's Little Money

New Sound (1380) 6:00 PM to 7:00 PM

Opening: "Lin Daiyu"

The Grand View Garden's scenery is very secluded, like a miniature Penglai Island. The thatched cottage in front is open and elegant, clearly indicating the beautiful scenery hidden in the Red Mansion. Hidden within is an unparalleled beauty, said to be more beautiful than flowers. Outside the Xiaoxiang Pavilion, the shadows of bamboo grow. The bitterness and sorrow are all like autumn. Her parents are far away, and she leans on the carved railing, filled with endless hatred. Roaming the garden, the scenery is secluded. Only the maids come and go. She is lazy to comb and wash her hair as usual, only fearing the dusk when the stars and moon are like hooks, hooking up the endless sorrow in her heart. Sadly, her loving mother passed away first, leaving the lonely girl to stay at her relatives' home. The old lady loves and cherishes her like a treasure, and the sisters' friendship is deep. Separated from her father by thousands of miles, her soul often circles over Yangzhou in dreams. Hoping for an imperial decree, she dances in colored clothes to express her filial piety. When will my lifelong wish be fulfilled? I burn incense and pray day and night. The most bitter is the matter of concern, and the two words "life-long" are not free. Although there will be a beautiful couple in the future, the old man of the moon has not yet planned. This feeling is shameful to say to outsiders, and she cries tears in the wind towards the moon. Her own infatuation, her own plan.

Shanghai City (900) Daily Program

Zhou Zhenyu's One Stick of Snow

Yuan Chang (1120) 12:45 AM to 1:30 AM

Opening: "Poor Woman's Sigh" (Mimi Collection Launch Issue)

Snowflakes dance and fill the sky. Xu Niang's heart is in a mess. Alone facing the cold window, she often sighs. She remembers being spoiled and raised in a farming family as a child. Her parents loved and cherished her like a treasure, and only the bright moon in the sky had not yet been taken. Three meals a day, she could choose what to eat. In winter, she wore brocade robes, and in summer, she wore silk gauze. Her parents arranged the marriage, truly hoping that the couple would live in harmony. Unexpectedly, her husband was a pleasure-seeking person. He did not do his job properly, indulging in flowers. Moreover, the elders in the family were addicted to opium, and the family business declined. Now, as the cold wind blows and the sky gets colder, she lacks clothes and food. The poor children cry sadly, wearing thin clothes with little cotton. Her heart is sad, and tears are shed. She hates that her husband's heart is too crooked, wasting money and seeking pleasure. Does he know that there is no rice or firewood at home? He laughs happily with those geishas, enjoying the lanterns and flowers, but she sacrifices her delicate body to work diligently. Sadly, there is not much money to help the family. Moreover, the children still need to study. She is a miserable and suffering woman in a skirt. Moreover, she has borrowed from relatives and neighbors, and she has no choice but to go back to her mother's house. Regardless of the cold weather, the frozen ground, and the uneven road.

Movie News

"Tiger Gets Married"

— Zhi Er

The Youth Association's Ninth Floor Is Another Grand Occasion

It's really fortunate. I had just returned from another location when I received a call from a friend saying, "The great Tiger," Zheng Junli, and Miss Huang Chen were getting married at the Youth Association building in Ba Xian Qiao.

Although I didn't receive a "We are getting married today..." notification, I had met "Tiger Face" a few times, so I put down all the work I was about to start and hired a car to go to the Youth Association. As the elevator took me up to the ninth floor, I suddenly thought of Tang Na and Lan Ping; Zhao Dan and Ye Lusi; Gu Eryi and Du Xiaojuan. When these pairs of actors got married, Zheng Junli and Li Qing were the matchmakers. (Li Qing has now joined Lianhua and has already started working on a segment of "Lianhua Symphony"). Many friends asked him that day when he would get married, but he just smiled and didn't answer because the "Standard Maid" was also present that day, accompanied by a "Southern Youth with Southern Hair." This situation was indeed too exciting for our Tiger.

But during the performance of "The Government Inspector," backstage at the Jincheng Grand Theater, introduced by Gu Menghu, he met Miss Huang Chen. From acquaintance to love, from love to marriage. Seeing Junli shaking hands with every guest with a radiant face, his friends seemed to feel a kind of "contagious" joy, a joy like drinking wine. Zhao Dan, Tang Na, Shi Chao, and even "Chamber of Commerce President" Yin Xiucen, were pushed by the wine to happily urge the bride and groom to report on their love story after Mr. Shen Junru's speech. The result was copying an old article, "And so on," thank you all!

To congratulate "lovers finally becoming family," someone initiated a signing, each person contributing one yuan to send the bride and groom dancing. So, thirty or forty people marched grandly to Lido. I left early because it was too late. Probably the joy of that evening cannot be described in words.

Finally, in addition to congratulating the newlyweds for their efforts in society, I also hope to hear the good news of another matchmaker when three pairs of actors get married in the near future. (The above is the newlyweds' signing ceremony)

Minxin News Bulletin

Li Keng studies daily at the nearby Peizhen Elementary School, waiting for the filming of "Gate of Flesh and Spirit" to begin. The filming work will also be carried out without hindering his studies, so as not to neglect his schoolwork.

"Gate of Flesh and Spirit," co-directed by Zhong Shigen and Zhao Ce, is expected to be released within the solar year and will create a new style for Chinese films.

"New Avenue," directed by Bu Wancang, started auspiciously on the 17th of this month. Originally, it was planned to go to Xuzhou and the surrounding areas to shoot exterior scenes first. Due to time constraints, it was decided to shoot several interior scenes first before departing.

The photography work of "New Humanism" is the responsibility of Zhuang Guojun and Shi Shiqing. Zhu Shutao also serves as the photography assistant and photographer for both "New Humanism" and "Gate of Flesh and Spirit."

Other important staff members for "New Humanism" have recently been announced:

Sound Recording: Li Geng, Lighting: Dai Yousheng, Scenery: Zhang Hanchen, Qin Wei, Props: Zhao Fuli, Stage Affairs and Makeup: Lin Jianming, Costumes and Props: Xiong Chun, Stage Management and Recorder: Dai Yanwan, Costume and Props Management: Ding Gaosheng.

At 5 p.m. on the 17th, the first day of "New Humanism," filming began on the interior scene of a Beijing restaurant. A total of thirty to forty staff and actors worked until 3 a.m.

Li Junqing, Huang Yunzhen, Qiu Yuanyuan, and Zhu Yaoting all play roles in "New Humanism."

The business department has been extremely busy recently with the distribution matters for the public performances of "Maternal Love" in various locations. "Maternal Love" is also awaiting public performance in Shanghai.

Qin Wei, an artist who studied in Japan, has recently been hired by Minxin Company after returning to China to work on art and design, and also to work on the scenery for "New Humanism."

There is a modern female teacher role in "Gate of Flesh and Spirit." In order to discover talent, Minxin plans to find and hire a newcomer to play the role, and it is currently in progress.
